<name>john liles</name>< Review>
I dont remember researching or deciding on cliffside, I was out of my mind and not hopeful that anything in my life could get better. Drugs and alcohol had stole everything from me, my wife, my, kids , my sense of purpose. Suicide had crossed my mind and I have never been in that dark of a place before. They say it gets worse, never better, this illness is progressive. I believed I could do it on my own. Even though I had failed 15 times to achieve this unrealistic dream.

Then came the experience that has changed my life, my stay at the sunset house. This exerience was eye opening. My first group I attended showed me I still had a lot to learn even though I had been through treatment 15 times before this. I met genuine people that showed me compassion and understanding, which take it from me, is not normal of any rehab I have been to. I knew this experience would be different. I was cared for and attended to. Any issue I shared was quickly resolved. Not only did the therapists that I saw frequently help me, they gave me what I needed to open up and change my thought proccess. The difference this time was being willing and open minded. I knew this was my last chance, I truly was defeated and had no belief that anything would ever work for me. I will be forever indebted to this amazing organization.

Please know if you are reading this, it works!!! I mean that from the bottom of my heart, I love everyone that I worked with and they all helped in some way. Recovery is possible and today I believe in myself and the dad I know I am. My children need me and I cannot wait to give them that father, the one who is present, sober and happy.

Thank you to the staff and the therapists, case managers, and most importantly the founder! Without this place I would quite possibly be dead today</Review>

My brother is very agitated and incoherent due to the lack of oxygen and has tried to leave the hospital twice, the first time he was lost for about 45 minutes why? Nobody knows and no info was given to us, the second time I believe he made almost out to the front door!  On April 29th we had a meeting with a social worker, the doctor attending my family and a nurse because we weren‚Äôt getting any answers or the right information.  Meeting went well, doctor and other staff attending were really nice, doctor gave us all the possible scenarios for both , brother and father we were reassured things will get better and the nurses will try to be more attentive. then I was introduced to the nurses that day, they told me that they were there to help in any way possible and they understood how difficult it is for families now days to deal with this pandemic.  Next day April 30th I called to check on my father‚Äôs health and I get a angry and ill manner nurse explaining the worst case scenario for my father and that it was time to make a decision weather to to put him on hospice or not because it was time and that he was not getting better, to hurry up and decide, so I call my family to decide and in the mean time some of my family members try calling to FaceTime to maybe say goodbye because it could be the last time we see him, like I said NOT ALL some nurses working that day get all angry because there are to many calls asking for his condition and it was not the case, the day before they have told us to call for FaceTime and it was going to be ok , that whole day was chaotic, we never had a single nurse helping willingly it was hard for me to let them know of my fathers wishes and to go on with all the medical services offered. Hannah was my fathers nurse that day sadly She was having a bad day but she had enough with my father so she decided to tell my father to stop wrestling with his oxygen mask and to cooperate otherwise he was going to die !  When I called that‚Äôs what I heard from her! I know their job is hard but so far I have 4 family members down with COVID two as you now know are at Simi hospital and this has been very hard for myself and family and the lack of empathy and support from some of the nurses it makes feel hopeless. We minimized the calling for FaceTime and I only call once a day to check his status, BUT EVERY MORNING BEFORE I CALL I  PRAY  TO GOD FOR A NICE NURSE to give us information without adding more drama or problems to our day. Every day is a scary day for the family because we don‚Äôt know that, when I call it might be the last day for my brother and father,  It‚Äôs stressful to call because I‚Äôm literally afraid of a hostile attitude from SOME OF TNE NURSES. Thanks to nurse Sherlyn very sweet I called on May first, night shift,  and Joe who was an angel and very helpful and made us feel better after the big chaos from April 30 Th.. so if you ask me right now about Simi Valley Adventist Hospital my answer will be no, don‚Äôt take you family or loved ones there , you‚Äôll soon be feeling hopeless. I will be contacting the manager from the nurses department. God bless and stay safe.</Text><pics>None< /pics>< Response>

<user>106356638422698642047< /user>< name>
Charles Sprinkle (Teravolt)< /name>
<Date>1536527575744<//Date><rate>5< /rate>< Review>
By far, the best place to vomit.

Many places can be recommended as a great place to have lunch, but not so many as the best place to lose it.  I visited this establishment with gastroenteritis.  The staff was very friendly in assisting me to check in, and the wait time was very short.  The triage nurse was also quick to provide a convenient vomit bag for my use while checking my vitals.  I have to say, the vomit bags were very nice with a stiff rim for rigidity and a pliable yet thick pouch.  Relief was provided fairly quickly with an intravenous anti-emetic and saline solution.  I enjoyed a quick nap while the medication dripped in and was ready to go sooner than I expected.

The ambience of the emergency room was very pleasant.  (I enjoy the faint aroma of isopropyl alcohol in the late evenings.)  Cleanliness was impeccable, as one might expect in a hospital,  and they even had the machine that goes "bing" to complete the full experience.

All in all, I would enthusiastically recommend this establishment for all of your vomiting needs.  (I hear they also do well with medical emergencies.)</Review>

<response>None< /response>< Text>
This hospital has changed greatly over the last few years, apparently, because when we moved here nine years ago, no one had anything nice to say about their own experiences there. We have never had a bad experience with this hospital. They were going through a massive remodel at the time of our first visit to the ER, and it's still continuing currently, although it's much farther along now and is more behind the scenes rather than taking over the ER, which is what we experienced in our first visit. But even at that visit, we were extremely impressed with the professionalism, and the compassion and kindness extended to us by everyone we encountered. My husband was taken care of quickly and thoroughly, and we never once felt that we were being rushed out the door after receiving inferior care. Since that visit, we've visited several times with various ailments, including a visit two years ago, where my husband was transported in an ambulance and was close to death from undiagnosed diabetes, with a blood sugar number of 2600. That is not a typo. He was there for over a week, and we are convinced that because of the superior care he received, his life was saved. To those who still think this hospital and it's staff are anything less than stellar, I think you will be pleasantly surprised the next time you visit.</Text>

<Text>Will temper some of my comments because it's under my name - gee, HIPAA protections not honored by Google?

Was brought to SVH for ankle fracture.  The ER staff was largely pleasant, helpful, & kind.  Bumping from one to two stars to give prop's to the ER folks.

Once admitted and taken to a regular room, started going downhill fast.  Had experiences like the night nurse bringing one of my med's at double normal dosage.  When I questioned it, she argued with me and said that it was what was ordered.  I said that didn't make it right.  Was to be 25 MG at night and 25 MG in the morning.  I insisted that I wouldn't take 50 MG.

She seemed confused & asked if I was refusing medication.  No, just the wrong amount.  She got the charge nurse in.  I explained situation.  Charge nurse says to RN to just break it in half.  RN tries, but says she's not strong enough, so hands it to charge nurse, and she does break it.  Hands it back to RN, who gives it to me.  Neither were wearing gloves.  I stated that this wasn't sterile.  They shrugged their shoulders and walked out of the room.

A number of other uncomfortable situations occurred, including not giving an anti-nausea med with narcotics for pain.  Thus, my body rejected the drugs and I became nauseous.  When reported to the nurses' station, was ignored.  Two hours later, I experienced what projectile vomiting is like.

After that, I took myself off narcotics and only had Tylenol for pain.  Didn't fully cut the pain, but was all my system could handle.

The last straw was the hospital's unilateral decision to send me to a skilled nursing facility for PT rehabilitation, when I insisted I could go home with proper help.  They shipped me off to a very sketchy place in the Valley without my approval.  That wasn't strictly their fault - turns out that most skilled nursing facilities in eastern Ventura County only take Medicare / Medical - not private PPO insurance.  What?!  That was a shocker.

Took me two days of proving to the system that I was capable of coming home.  Should there be a next time I need a hospital, will go to Los Robles or West Hills.<//Text><Pictures>None</Pictures>< Resp>
